<h1 class="bookTitle" id="bookTitle" itemprop="name">
      And Then There Were None
</h1>
<div class="stacked" id="bookAuthors">
<span class="by smallText">by</span>
<span itemprop="author" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
<a class="authorName" href="http://www.goodreads.com/author/show/123715.Agatha_Christie" itemprop="url"><span itemprop="name">Agatha Christie</span></a>
</span>
</div>

<div class="readable stacked" id="description" style="right:0">
<span id="freeTextContainer16653946420297425077">First, there were ten - a curious assortment of strangers summoned as weekend guests to a private island off the coast of Devon. Their host, an eccentric millionaire unknown to all of them, is nowhere to be found. All that the guests have in common is a wicked past they're unwilling to reveal - and a secret that will seal their fate. For each has been marked for murder. On</span>
<span id="freeText16653946420297425077" style="display:none">First, there were ten - a curious assortment of strangers summoned as weekend guests to a private island off the coast of Devon. Their host, an eccentric millionaire unknown to all of them, is nowhere to be found. All that the guests have in common is a wicked past they're unwilling to reveal - and a secret that will seal their fate. For each has been marked for murder. One by one they fall prey. Before the weekend is out, there will be none. And only the dead are above suspicion.</span>

<a href="/user/show/32039014-midnight-anderson">Midnight Anderson</a>
</span>
<span class="communityAnswerText">
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">i liked the book and the twists kept me interested and guessing whom was the murderer. Its the ending that I felt was a bit too much for myself...the<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">i liked the book and the twists kept me interested and guessing whom was the murderer. Its the ending that I felt was a bit too much for myself...the story, the epilogue, AND the murderer's manuscript. nice way to wrap up the story but it took ALL the mystery out of the mystery and my initial response to the ending was dull and numb by the manuscript<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

All the characters are easy to remember, witch can be hard to do for a book<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">No. The writing can get a little weird at times, but it's a good book. All the characters are easy to remember, witch can be hard to do for a book with a lot of characters.   <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div class="section firstReview">
<div class="review nosyndicate" id="review_101058640" itemprop="reviews" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
<link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/101058640" itemprop="url"/>
<a class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3672777-nataliya" title="Nataliya"><img alt="Nataliya" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1395089173p2/3672777.jpg"/></a>
<div class="left bodycol">
<div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
<a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/101058640?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate">Oct 31, 2012</a>
<a class="user" href="/user/show/3672777-nataliya" title="Nataliya">Nataliya</a>

        rated it
        <a class=" staticStars stars_4" title="really liked it">4 of 5 stars</a>
<span class="greyText"> · </span>
<a class="lightGreyText" href="/book/show/9723667-and-then-there-were-none" title="Paperback 9780062073488">review of another edition</a>
<div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
                <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=i-also-saw-the-film">i-also-saw-the-film</a>, 
                <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=2012-reads">2012-reads</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="reviewText stacked">
<span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer101058640" style="">
<span id="freeTextContainer235915001110741958"><br>This lovely mystery book is first and foremost about the administration of the long-overdue justice, right? At least that's what the mastermind behind it all believes.<br><br>But the question is - <strong>who has the right to decide what justice is?</strong> And who is to decide what punishment serves the crime? And is perceived justice at all costs the ultimate goal, or is it the frequently pointless work of a maniac? As a matter of fact, what is justice after all?<br><br><img class="escapedImg" src="https://p.gr-assets.com/540x540/fit/hostedimages/1380334544/693814.jpg" width="400"><br><br>I think the story of this book (<a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:And_Then_There_Were_None_First_Edition_Cover_1939.jpg" rel="nofollow">the one that may win th</a></br></br></img></br></br></br></br></br></span>
<span id="freeText235915001110741958" style="display:none"><br>This lovely mystery book is first and foremost about the administration of the long-overdue justice, right? At least that's what the mastermind behind it all believes.<br><br>But the question is - <strong>who has the right to decide what justice is?</strong> And who is to decide what punishment serves the crime? And is perceived justice at all costs the ultimate goal, or is it the frequently pointless work of a maniac? As a matter of fact, what is justice after all?<br><br><img class="escapedImg" src="https://p.gr-assets.com/540x540/fit/hostedimages/1380334544/693814.jpg" width="400"><br><br>I think the story of this book (<a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:And_Then_There_Were_None_First_Edition_Cover_1939.jpg" rel="nofollow">the one that may win the contest for the most offensive original title, after all</a>) is familiar to most readers. It is a lovely and fascinating idea. Ten people are lured onto a remote island under false pretenses just to realize that they are all about to be punished by death for the 'crimes' that they have committed in the past and have gotten away with. Killed in a manner predicted by a silly yet ominous children's poem with the conclusion of <em>"... and then there were none"</em>. What's more, they come to realize that the mastermind - or maniac? - has to be among them. <strong>And the (very polite, in the traditional British way) game of survival begins, complete with all the necessary societal rituals¹ and classism² that are not disposed of even under the threat of imminent demise.</strong><br><blockquote>¹The politeness and overt show of respect to one another even in the face of imminent murder by someone in their midst - because, of course, you would not want to offend anyone. Continuing to socialize and take meals together. Insisting on chivalry when a woman could be the murderer just as well as a man (<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[this viewing of women as shrinking violets was what cost Philip Lombard his life in the end! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>) - these are just some of the examples.<br><br>² Just think of everyone expecting the impeccable service by the butler even though HIS WIFE JUST DIED! Everyone deciding to stick together and be careful - but never including the servants in it. The belief by some that people of 'proper class' would be incapable of murder (<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Doctor Amstrong becomes a victim of just this reasoning <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>). The list can go on and on. And all of these assumptions prove to be wrong.</br></br></blockquote><br><img class="escapedImg" src="https://p.gr-assets.com/540x540/fit/hostedimages/1380334544/693815.jpg" width="400"><br><br>And as, despite the precautions, the number of people trapped on the island continues to decline, the uneasy tension sets in, and the impeccable facades begin to crack.<br><blockquote>"<em>The oth­ers went up­stairs, a slow unwilling pro­ces­sion. If this had been an old house, with creak­ing wood, and dark shad­ows, and heav­ily pan­elled walls, there might have been an eerie feel­ing. But this house was the essence of moder­ni­ty. There were no dark corners - ​no possi­ble slid­ing pan­els - it was flood­ed with elec­tric light - everything was new and bright and shining. There was nothing hid­den in this house, noth­ing con­cealed. It had no at­mo­sphere about it. Some­how, that was the most fright­en­ing thing of all. They ex­changed good-​nights on the up­per land­ing. Each of them went in­to his or her own room, and each of them automatical­ly, al­most with­out con­scious thought, locked the door.</em>"</blockquote><br>The story is captivating and very smart, and the ending had me baffled for a bit the first time I read it. It has a neat resolution despite an obvious plot hole <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ - Wargrave's brains will be all over the bed on which he was NOT supposed to have died! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. It's an enjoyable read to say the least. <br><br><strong>But what made me unsettled both of the times I read it was the nagging question of justice, as I mentioned above.</strong> Yes, on one hand, it's almost poetic justice to punish the criminals who thought they got away with it. On the other hand, is eye-for-an-eye the best way to get even? And who's to judge, anyway? Who is either conceited enough or deranged enough to assume that he has the right and the moral authority to determine guilt and the extent of punishment just like that?<br><br><img class="escapedImg" src="https://p.gr-assets.com/540x540/fit/hostedimages/1380334544/693816.jpg" width="400"><br><br><strong>Don't get me wrong - the people accused on the island are undeniably guilty</strong> <em>(even though it's not necessarily murder as we think of for some of them - Vera Claythorne is really guilty of neglect, albeit with a desire to kill, and Emily Brent is pretty much guilty of being a judgmental über-righteous heartless prude)</em>. But the degree of their guilt varies quite significantly in my perception, and it does not always coincide with what their 'unknown' judge/executioner thinks <em>(running two children over with a car and feeling no remorse is to me worse than firing a pregnant servant who then goes on to kill herself, for instance)</em>. <strong>And is arbitrarily and single-handedly determining their guilt and doling out punishments not just as much (or even much worse) or a crime than they have committed?</strong> Conceited, self-righteous crime? Decide for yourself. <br><br><img class="escapedImg" src="https://p.gr-assets.com/540x540/fit/hostedimages/1380334544/693817.jpg" width="400"><br><br>Speaking of <strong>guilt</strong> - this novel has quite a bit to say on this subject. You see, many of the characters have already been judged and condemned by their own selves. Vera Claythorne and General Macarthur both are tormented by their guilt (and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Vera actually becomes a direct victim of it, after all, becoming her own executioner in the rather creepy and effective scene <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>). Interestingly, others, no less guilty, are not tormented by their conscience at all. But ultimately this does not matter at all for their survival; only the fact that they were deemed guilty (<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[except for Vera, as I mentioned above. Remorseless Philip Lombard would not have cracked like she did, had he been the one holding the revolver a few minutes earlier <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>). <strong>So should being tormented by guilt versus a cold-blooded killer factor at all in the administration of justice?</strong><br><br>These are the thoughts that kept running through my head as I was reading this excellent non-traditional critically-acclaimed specimen of mystery literature. And therefore bravo to Miss Christie for making me think and care - and not just mindlessly flipping pages to get to the bottom of the whodunit. Because <em>'WHO'</em> was much less important to me than <em>'HOW'</em> and <em>'WHY'</em> - especially <em>'WHY'</em>. <br><br>For all of this, I give it the unflinching <strong>guilt-free 4 stars.</strong><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></br></br></br></br></br></br></img></br></br></br></br></img></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></img></br></br></br></br></img></br></br></br></br></br></span>
<a data-text-id="235915001110741958" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
</span>

<div class="review" id="review_154124122" itemprop="reviews" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
<link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/154124122" itemprop="url"/>
<a class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/110812-kinga" title="Kinga"><img alt="Kinga" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1372944049p2/110812.jpg"/></a>
<div class="left bodycol">
<div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
<a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/154124122?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate">Sep 18, 2012</a>
<a class="user" href="/user/show/110812-kinga" title="Kinga">Kinga</a>

        rated it
        <a class=" staticStars stars_4" title="really liked it">4 of 5 stars</a>
<span class="greyText"> · </span>
<a class="lightGreyText" href="/book/show/6251563-and-then-there-were-none" title="Kindle Edition ">review of another edition</a>
</div>
<div class="reviewText stacked">
<span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer154124122" style="">
<span id="freeTextContainer1620641558437875568">Before I begin I would like to apologise for my use of the N word in this review. <br>It is necessary, I promise.<br><br>This book was originally published in UK under a charming title of "Ten Little Niggers". When it came to the US version in the 40's someone decided that 'Ten Little Niggers' is not the most marketable title for a book so they changed it to 'Ten Little Indians' (as it was still ok to call Native Americans Indians then).<br>Only years after someone decided that  neither 'Niggers', nor 'Indians'</br></br></br></br></span>
<span id="freeText1620641558437875568" style="display:none">Before I begin I would like to apologise for my use of the N word in this review. <br>It is necessary, I promise.<br><br>This book was originally published in UK under a charming title of "Ten Little Niggers". When it came to the US version in the 40's someone decided that 'Ten Little Niggers' is not the most marketable title for a book so they changed it to 'Ten Little Indians' (as it was still ok to call Native Americans Indians then).<br>Only years after someone decided that  neither 'Niggers', nor 'Indians' is a fortunate choice of words for the title so it was changed to 'And Then There Were None' - the last line of the nursery rhyme which in this new version was called 'Ten Boy Soldiers'.<br><br>This is the version that I read and I must say I am glad. I think I would be rather uncomfortable reading something called 'The Little Niggers', which takes place on 'Nigger Island' (how did Christie want to pull this off? 'Nigger Island' off the Devon coast? Really? How?).<br><br>The premise, I am sure you know, is this: ten people end up cut off from the world on a tiny island. One of them is a murderer and people keep dying as in the nursery rhyme. Every person on the island has a secret and is guilty of a murder. It's the kind of murder where law is helpless. Nothing can be proven. This is why they found themselves on that island, at the mercy of a prototype 'Jigsaw' madman who decided justice must be done.<br><br>The premise requires the structure of the novel to be very organised and clean cut. I felt that it was only right for me to approach the reading of it in an equally disciplined way. I took five sheets of papers and divide each in half, thus ending up with ten cards, one for each character.<br><br>And I continued to dilligently fill them out with all the details I learnt about the characters until about halfway through the book when I became too engrossed, frightened and nervous. I already had an inkling as to who the murderer was and was petrified I would be murdered in my sleep as well. The situation was very serious and I had to invite all my teddy bears back to my bed, so they could protect me.<br><br>I grew to like two of the characters - the sentiment, I think, I shared with Christie as she liked them so, she killed them last.<br><br>This was my second Christie, and the first proper one. The first one I read was a bit of a mishap spy novel, so Christie's brilliance wasn't as apparent as it was in 'And Then There Were None'. <br><br><br>4.5 stars<br><br>PS&gt; Thanks to karen I have just found this page -  <a href="http://www.betterbooktitles.com" rel="nofollow">betterbooktitles</a><br><br>And here is their take on Ms Christie:<br><img class="escapedImg" src="https://p.gr-assets.com/540x540/fit/hostedimages/1380346919/701296.jpg"/></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></span>
<a data-text-id="1620641558437875568" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
</span>

<span id="freeText16884449348764360845" style="display:none">Oh I didn't know that. <div class="section">
<div class="review" id="review_904892286" itemprop="reviews" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
<link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/904892286" itemprop="url"/>
<a class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/665584-alejandro" title="Alejandro"><img alt="Alejandro" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1328672389p2/665584.jpg"/></a>
<div class="left bodycol">
<div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
<a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/904892286?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate">Jul 23, 2014</a>
<a class="user" href="/user/show/665584-alejandro" title="Alejandro">Alejandro</a>

        rated it
        <a class=" staticStars stars_5" title="it was amazing">5 of 5 stars</a>
<span class="greyText"> · </span>
<a class="lightGreyText" href="/book/show/9723667-and-then-there-were-none" title="Paperback 9780062073488">review of another edition</a>
<div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
                <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=novel">novel</a>, 
                <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
                <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=detective">detective</a>, 
                <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=horror">horror</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="reviewText stacked">
<span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer904892286" style="">
<span id="freeTextContainer11074306508350334107"><strong>Extraordinary and gripping novel!</strong><br><br>I knew that the best way to start reading the literary work by Agatha Christie was choosing her most known book. <em>And There were none</em> is the best-selling mystery novel of all time with 100 million of copies, and the fifth book in the list comprehending all genres. <strong>That</strong> is something to give to Agatha Christie the respect that she deserves.<br><br>Initially this novel on UK was titled <em>Ten Little Niggers</em>, only because the original nursery rhyme was called that but it was obv</br></br></br></br></span>
<span id="freeText11074306508350334107" style="display:none"><strong>Extraordinary and gripping novel!</strong><br><br>I knew that the best way to start reading the literary work by Agatha Christie was choosing her most known book. <em>And There were none</em> is the best-selling mystery novel of all time with 100 million of copies, and the fifth book in the list comprehending all genres. <strong>That</strong> is something to give to Agatha Christie the respect that she deserves.<br><br>Initially this novel on UK was titled <em>Ten Little Niggers</em>, only because the original nursery rhyme was called that but it was obviously seen as racist, then in USA was decided to change the title to <em>Ten Little Indians</em>, but again obviously as seen as racist again, so at the end the title was changed to <em>And There were none</em>, and the nursery rhyme inside the book was changed to "Ten Little Soldiers", curiously enough none member of any army so far as pointed out as racist that final change. I mean, the title was just because a widely known nursery rhyme and none character on the book was afro-american or native-american. <br><br>To this, I want to comment that it's lucky that not many children would had more nightmares since a lot of nursery rhymes have truly scary lyrics. No wonder in stuff like <em>A Nightmare on Elm Street</em> and <em>Saphire and Steel</em> were used nursery rhymes with truly scary effects.<br><br>Returning to the novel, it was a remarkable reading. Great atmosphere where you feel as trapped as those people on that island.<br><br>I want to comment that at some point I figured it out who was the murderer, don't worry, I won't tell it, and I have no doubt that some would say: "Oh, sure! I believe you Sherlock!". However I do indeed discovered it. This is not my first mystery story. I have read several books in the genre and I have watched a lot of TV shows like <em>Murder, She Wrote</em>,  <em>Columbo</em>, <em>Criminal Minds</em>, <em>CSI: Miami</em>, etc... And while that doesn't turn me into a detective, in my defense, I knew who was only because I focused on the "why" and not the "how" that certainly I didn't know that. You can say that I did an amateur criminal profile and that helped me to have a suspect of my own that it resulted true. Also, I had some advantage for being Spanish speaking since there is a clue that only can be detected due that not matter that I read the novel on English, but taking in account the very detail that it's indeed a printed novel, I catched something and putting together some clues. Well, I figured it out. Believe or not. It doesn't matter.<br><br>Anyway, I think that many of the fun of reading this kind of mystery novels is trying to figure out the culprit during the process of reading the book. Not matter if you guess right or not, always it's rewarding when the mystery is explained. A delicious way to make your neurons to exercise.<br><br>Again, knowing who was, or at least thinking that I knew who was, since obviously I couldn't confirm it until reading the whole book, it didn't help me to know how everything was made until it was explained on the novel. Definitely, Agatha Christie is the queen of mystery!<br><br>Certainly, this novel isn't only a marvellous detective mystery book but also a truly scary horror story. Priceless setting for a scenario and fantastic twisted character developing.<br><br><strong>
<u>Appendix: (July 23rd, 2014)</u>
</strong><br><br>The clue that I found thanks that I am a born Spanish-language speaker:<br><br><strong>WARNING!!!  WARNING!!!  WARNING!!!  WARNING!!!</strong><br><br>Read <strong>ONLY</strong> if you already read the novel, since this is a mega-spoiler telling who the culprit is!<br><br><em>I seldom put spoilers in my reviews, but I wrote this appendix basically since I was contacted by several readers asking me about the "big clue" and well, while I don't mind to share it, well, also I don't want to find out later that it was written down in some other review as theirs, taking in account that it seems that only me were the one who noticed that.</em><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Ok, the big fuzz about the clue that I found is that the first character that you find in the novel is Mr. Justice Wargrave on the chapter one, you may say: "So what?", well, the mysterious couple who invited to all guests, the initials of both names of them are U.N.O., in the imaginary woman is "Una Nancy Owen" and the supposed husband is "U.N. Owen. U.N.O. that in Spanish can be spelled just like "uno" which means "one" on English. Maybe that a coincidence, but with Agatha Christie nothing can be left to chance, so I think that may be a clue targeted to the readers with knowledge about Spanish language. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></span>
<a data-text-id="11074306508350334107" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
</span>

<div class="review" id="review_722285742" itemprop="reviews" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
<link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/722285742" itemprop="url"/>
<a class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13592557-mohammed-arabey" title="Mohammed Arabey"><img alt="Mohammed Arabey" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1364338486p2/13592557.jpg"/></a>
<div class="left bodycol">
<div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
<a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/722285742?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate">Feb 07, 2015</a>
<a class="user" href="/user/show/13592557-mohammed-arabey" title="Mohammed Arabey">Mohammed Arabey</a>

        rated it
        <a class=" staticStars stars_5" title="it was amazing">5 of 5 stars</a>
<span class="greyText"> · </span>
<a class="lightGreyText" href="/book/show/181133.And_Then_There_Were_None" title="Paperback 9780007136834">review of another edition</a>
</div>
<div class="reviewText stacked">
<span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer722285742" style="">
<span id="freeTextContainer607015776694398789">يجب أن أعترف أن ضيق أفقي هو مامنعني من بدء القراءة لعالم أجاثا كريستي<br>فمنذ صغري لم تبهرني أغلفه قصصها المترجمة للعربية<br>كما أن معرفة والدي لافلامها بل وقراءة والدتي لروايتها منذ صغرها جعلني أشعر أن التشويق بهذه القصص صار "موضة قديمة" وأكيد ألغازها ستكون مكشوفة لي<br>ناهيك عن مقولة "لابد أنه الخادم هو من فعلها.. كقصص أجاثا كريستي" جعلتني <br>متشككا أن الحل بعد كل هذه السنوات صار نمطيا بقصص أجاثا كريستي<br>فلماذا أقرأ لها؟..لم يعد هناك شئ<br><img alt="" class="escapedImg" height="222" src="https://p.gr-assets.com/540x540/fit/hostedimages/1380437017/883613.jpg" width="394"><strong>
<em>
<blockquote>
<br>عشر عساكر صغار ذهبوا الي العشاء<br>اختنق احدهم ..ثم تبقي تسعه</br></br></blockquote>
</em>
</strong><br>الي ان جائتني د</br></img></br></br></br></br></br></br></span>
<span id="freeText607015776694398789" style="display:none">يجب أن أعترف أن ضيق أفقي هو مامنعني من بدء القراءة لعالم أجاثا كريستي<br>فمنذ صغري لم تبهرني أغلفه قصصها المترجمة للعربية<br>كما أن معرفة والدي لافلامها بل وقراءة والدتي لروايتها منذ صغرها جعلني أشعر أن التشويق بهذه القصص صار "موضة قديمة" وأكيد ألغازها ستكون مكشوفة لي<br>ناهيك عن مقولة "لابد أنه الخادم هو من فعلها.. كقصص أجاثا كريستي" جعلتني <br>متشككا أن الحل بعد كل هذه السنوات صار نمطيا بقصص أجاثا كريستي<br>فلماذا أقرأ لها؟..لم يعد هناك شئ<br><img alt="" class="escapedImg" height="222" src="https://p.gr-assets.com/540x540/fit/hostedimages/1380437017/883613.jpg" width="394"><strong>
<em>
<blockquote>
<br>عشر عساكر صغار ذهبوا الي العشاء<br>اختنق احدهم ..ثم تبقي تسعه</br></br></blockquote>
</em>
</strong><br>الي ان جائتني دعوه..دعوه لقراءه احد كتب اجاثا كريستي لانها في قائمه اعلي الكتب مبيعا متفوقه علي الالاف كتب التشويق والجريمه!!! مما جعلني متشوقا لمعرفه السبب<br>تلك الدعوه كانت في ويكابيديا..قائمه اعلي الكتب مبيعا في التاريخ<br><br><img alt="description" class="escapedImg" height="231" src="https://p.gr-assets.com/540x540/fit/hostedimages/1423330375/13607951.jpg" width="400"><br><strong>
<em>
<blockquote>تسع عساكر صغار سهروا لوقت متاخر<br>نام احدهم طويلا..ثم تبقي ثمانيه</br></blockquote>
</em>
</strong><br>هذا ما جعلني متشوقا لمعرفه سر هذه الروايه..التي تفوقت في اثارتها وتشويقها علي الكثير من اقرانها في المبيعات..وحتي  تفوقها علي كل روايات اجاثا كريستي<br>وقد كان...وبدأت في الكتاب<br><strong>
<em>
<blockquote>ثماني عساكر صغار سافروا لديفون<br>قرر احدهم البقاء..ثم تبقي سبعه</br></blockquote>
</em>
</strong><br>كنت مصمما اولا ألا اقرأ اي ريفيو عن الروايه ولا ألمح حتي صفحات الافلام المبنية عنها<br>فقد كنت مصمما ان اعرف اللغز وأحله بنفسي قبل انتهاء صفحات الروايه<br><strong>
<em>
<blockquote>سبع عساكر صغار يشطرون الاخشاب<br>شطر احدهم نفسه نصفين..ثم تبقي سته</br></blockquote>
</em>
</strong><strong><br>ومنذ الفصل الاول وجدت نفسي في روايه متعدده الشخصيات..متعدده وجهات النظر..ثماني اشخاص لا يعرفون بعضهم بعضا..متجهون نحو قصر بجزيره..غامض صاحبه..وغامض السبب الحقيقي وراء ذهابهم او دعوتهم.. غامض دعواتهم للقصر شيئا ما..الا انهم قرروا الذهاب ايا كان<br><br>متباينين..غير متناسقين عمريا ولا فكريا ولا كمستوي اجتماعي او مادي او حتي وطيفي...مشتركين في غموض ماضيهم..غموض دوافعهم<br>ليذهبوا ويقابلوا زوجين من الخدم غامضين ايضا..لايعرفون شيئا عن سيدهم ولم يروه حتي الان..بل ويكادوا يجزمون بينهم وبين انفسهم بغرابه ذلك الحشد الغريب الغير متناسق,الغير متجانس بين الشخصيات امامهم<br><br>يبدأ العشاء علي مائده يزينها تماثيل صغيره لعشر عساكر..وتبدأ الاحداث الغريبه في البدء منذ اوائل الفصول<br><br><img alt="description" class="escapedImg" height="297" src="https://p.gr-assets.com/540x540/fit/hostedimages/1380437017/883615.jpg" width="396"/></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></strong><br><strong>
<em>
<blockquote>ست عساكر صغار يلعبون جوار خليه نحل<br>لسعت نحله غاضبه احدهم..ثم تبقي خمسه</br></blockquote>
</em>
</strong><br>اتهامات غريبه يسمعونها تخص ماضي كل شخصيه من العشر شخصيات<br>والمفترض انهم وحدهم بالجزيره<br><br>ونعم..كما تقول الاسطوره بعد العشاء الاول مباشره..يختنق احدهم..كحادث مدبر؟ انتحار؟ جريمه قتل؟<br><br>ثم يتبقي تسعه..ليتفكروا في الامر<br><strong>
<em>
<blockquote>خمس عساكر صغار يذهبون للحكم<br>تحفظ علي حكم احدهم..ثم تبقي اربعه</br></blockquote>
</em>
</strong><br><br>تتوالي الاحداث..في ترقب..من صاحب الدعوه؟ ماحقيقه الاتهامات؟<br>كان هناك 10 تماثيل عساكر في وسط مائده الطعام..لماذا صار فقط تسع بعد وفاه احدهم؟<br><strong>
<em>
<blockquote>اربع عساكر صغار يذهبون لبحر<br>تخدع سمكه حمراء احدهم..ثم تبقي ثلاثه</br></blockquote>
</em>
</strong><br>حتي وان تبقي ثلاثه..لن تعرف من يقوم بهذا<br>هل هو احدهم؟ هل هناك احد غيرهم العشره مختبئ في مكان ما؟<br>هذا لا يمكن ان يكون صحيحا..لقد فتشنا المكان جيدا.حتي الجثث ..اهو حلم؟عذرا ..كابوس؟؟<br><strong>
<em>
<blockquote>ثلاث عساكر صغار يذهبون لحديقه الحيوانات<br>اخذ الدب احدهم..ثم تبقي أثنان</br></blockquote>
</em>
</strong><br><strong> وتتغلغل الروايه بعبقريه داخل نفس الانسان ..وغريزته الحيوانيه في البقاء..والدفاع عن نفسه<br>فبمجرد تناقص عدد الشخصيات تبدأ تصرفاتهم في الريبه والشك والخوف وكانهم فعلا حيوانات مفترسه<br><br>ستشعر كم ابرعت اجاثا كريستي ملكه الجريمه في تصوير باختصار موجز رعب وهلع النفس البشريه في مواجهه المجهول..وفي الشك في الغرباء حتي تصل لدرجه البارانويا<br><br>بل ستجعلك في لحظات في اواخر الروايه تشعر بنفس البرانويا والترقب والفزع كانك التالي لقد كنت "بدون مبالغه" احبس انفاسي في بعض الاجزاء الاخيره<br><strong><em><blockquote>اثنان عساكر صغار جلسا في الشمس<br>اصيب احدهم بضربه شمس..ثم تبقي واحد</br></blockquote></em></strong><br><br>روايه واحده نالت كل التقديرات المتميزه لاجاثا كريستي..رفعت لها القبعات منذ اول صدورها في الثلاثينات من القرن الماضي وحتي الان<br>وبالرغم من ان انتاج افلام عن الروايه لم يحدث من فتره طويله الا انه صدرت لعبه "فيديوجيم" للكمبيوتر في 2004<br><br>روايه واحده ستجعلك تتوحد في قراءتها مع الابطال..ستظن انك عرفت شيئا ما -وبصعوبه- وسيتضح خطأك بعد بضع صفحات<br>حتي تأتي النهايه المكتوبه بحرفيه اجاثا كريستي المتوجه عالميا كملكه الجريمه<br><br>روايه واحده التي اثنت مؤلفتها علي حرفيتها بنفسها في مقدمه الروايه لمجهودها في جعل جرائم القتل مقبوله وحل الجرائم مقنع<br>وملاءم للاسطوره<br><br>اسطوره العشر عساكر الصغار<br><strong><em><blockquote>عسكري واحد صغير تبقي وحيدا..ذهب وشنق نفسه<br>ثم لم يتبق احد<br>And Then There Were None</br></br></blockquote></em></strong><br><br>نعم لم يتبق احد..ولكن تبقي لي تراث اجاثا كريستي لاقرأ فيه من وقت لاخر<br>تراث يقرأ لاجيال..ليتعرف به علي افضل ماكتب في مجال التشويق والاثاره وعالم الجريمه<br><img alt="description" class="escapedImg" height="228" src="https://p.gr-assets.com/540x540/fit/hostedimages/1380437017/883616.jpg" width="380"><br/></img></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></strong><br>محمد العربي<br>من 17 سبتمبر 2013<br>الي 23 سبتمبر 2013<br><a href="http://www.khassab.net/news/?p=2917" rel="nofollow">مقال أخترنا لك عن اعلي مبيعات الروايات منهم ثم لم يبق أحد</a></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></img></br></br></br></br></img></br></br></br></br></br></br></span>

<div class="review nosyndicate" id="review_90508521" itemprop="reviews" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
<link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/90508521" itemprop="url"/>
<a class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1630617-moira-russell" title="Moira Russell"><img alt="Moira Russell" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1256449807p2/1630617.jpg"/></a>
<div class="left bodycol">
<div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
<a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/90508521?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate">May 14, 2010</a>
<a class="user" href="/user/show/1630617-moira-russell" title="Moira Russell">Moira Russell</a>

          added it


          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
<a class="lightGreyText" href="/book/show/231622.And_Then_There_Were_None" title="Paperback 9780312979478">review of another edition</a>
<div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
                <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1630617-moira-russell?shelf=2010-50-new-books-challenge">2010-50-new-books-challenge</a>, 
                <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1630617-moira-russell?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="reviewText stacked">
<span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer90508521" style="">
<span id="freeTextContainer2662931007908175113">I admit I am a late, reluctant and suspicious convert to Christie. I avoided her studiously as an adolescent, because dozens and dozens of her paperbacks were always on sale with equally cheap indistinguishable romances and other 'women's books,' and I wanted no part of those. I read Chandler, not Christie; Hammett, not Sayers; James, not Marsh. I even read a few <em>Spillane</em> books, for Chrissakes, at a friend's urging (UGH), but still no Christie. Those endless TV adaptations, with the dotty Miss M</span>
<span id="freeText2662931007908175113" style="display:none">I admit I am a late, reluctant and suspicious convert to Christie. I avoided her studiously as an adolescent, because dozens and dozens of her paperbacks were always on sale with equally cheap indistinguishable romances and other 'women's books,' and I wanted no part of those. I read Chandler, not Christie; Hammett, not Sayers; James, not Marsh. I even read a few <em>Spillane</em> books, for Chrissakes, at a friend's urging (UGH), but still no Christie. Those endless TV adaptations, with the dotty Miss Marple and dorky Poirot, didn't help either. I had her books written off - predictable - cozy - tricksy - unreal - <em>feminine.</em> I liked Patricia Cornwell and <em>noir.</em> Show me a grisly procedural and I'll sink into it like a warm bath.<br><br>The result of this prejudice, of course, was that I never saw what was actually there and only cheated myself. But matters weren't helped when I took a (delightful) genre studies course in graduate school <em>(The Singing Sands, Ashenden, Knight's Gambit, An Unsuitable Job for a Woman,</em> Poe, Doyle....) and we had to read <em>The Murder of Roger Ackroyd,</em> about whom legendary snob Edmund Wilson famously asked: Who Cares? Not me. (Not that I cared for Wilson either.) I <em>hated</em> that book.<br><br>But during that course I ran across something interesting. For my final topic I chose the work of P.D. James (and read all of her books published up til then - through <em>Original Sin</em> - in about a month; dizzying but v fun) and you couldn't miss emblazoned on all her paperbacks at the time, THE NEW QUEEN OF CRIME, SHE USURPS CHRISTIE'S THRONE, CAGEMATCH BETWEEN PHYLLIS AND AGATHA, TWO BITCHES ENTER ONE NOVELIST LEAVES, &amp;c &amp;c you get the picture. This was mainly very stupid marketing because James and Christie have almost nothing in common (even tho James's first, derivative novel had the classic locked-room scenario). But I read a lot of interviews with James, and while she was polite about Christie (well, she's British) I sensed something else: respect. Apparently her tone's changed a bit in her most recent nonfiction book about mysteries, but then she said something like: 'She is a conjurer with those cards, and each time you think you know which one she is turning face-up, and each time you are wrong.' <br><br>Well, now that was interesting. <em>Every</em> time? And I discovered the answer is, yes, pretty much. Call it a trick, call it a gimmick, call it masterful puzzle-plotting, call it a kind of genius, whatever it is, it's frighteningly consistent. It is what Stephen King terms the 'gotta' in <em>Misery</em> raised almost to an art form. It is what Magnus Eisengrim describes in Robertson Davies' <em>World of Wonders</em> as what makes a great magician: 'A man who can stand stark naked in the middle of a crowd and keep it gaping for an hour while he manipulates a few coins, or cards, or billiard balls.'<br><br>This would have been a far, far better book for me to read in that class that was almost fifteen years ago now (gosh). For one thing, it has a sharp, strong, original female central character (she's not quite a heroine); its gimmick is equally as good as Ackroyd's; and it is a dazzling distinctive example of the One-Of-Us-is-a-Murderer-But-Which-One plot. Even better, there is no trace of that horrific Socratic bore Hercule Poirot or any of his little grey cells. For all that critics harp on Christie's cardboard characters and outlandish setups, this book depends largely on characterization and atmosphere. Each of the ten people brought to a deserted, barren island is guilty to a greater or lesser degree of causing the death of another person, and the book becomes almost a meditation on - what is guilt? What is responsibility? The murderer isn't just randomly cutting people down, but manipulating them, and enjoying it. Even if they are all as guilty as she or he thinks they are, do they deserve to be picked off and psychologically tortured? What justifies passing sentence on someone else? These are not easy questions and Christie does not give easy answers.<br><br>(Also trying to write a spoiler-free review of this is hard, yeesh.)</br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></span>
<a data-text-id="2662931007908175113" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
</span>
</div>

        rated it
        <a class=" staticStars stars_5" title="it was amazing">5 of 5 stars</a>

<div class="reviewText stacked">
<span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer134293107" style="">
<span id="freeTextContainer17353628289611327466">I'm a big lover of Agatha Christie, she has written some fantastic murder mysteries and her stories never get tiring. But this is the one that just comes out on top every time.<br><br>It partly, and quite amusingly, reminds me of that old American murder mystery in Sunset Beach. Basically, they're the only ones on this island and someone is killing them off one by one in accordance with the Ten Little Indians rhyme . And I swear I never saw it coming, and I'm usually very good at it. It's just a very cl</br></br></span>
<span id="freeText17353628289611327466" style="display:none">I'm a big lover of Agatha Christie, she has written some fantastic murder mysteries and her stories never get tiring. But this is the one that just comes out on top every time.<br><br>It partly, and quite amusingly, reminds me of that old American murder mystery in Sunset Beach. Basically, they're the only ones on this island and someone is killing them off one by one in accordance with the Ten Little Indians rhyme . And I swear I never saw it coming, and I'm usually very good at it. It's just a very clever novel, full of mystery and suspense and easily quite frightening at times.<br><br>I like how Agatha Christie doesn't have to write a 500 page novel with a massive back story, her mysteries are very simply put together but always clever and hard to decipher. I would recommend this book to everyone.</br></br></br></br></span>

<a class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/171921-halfino-berry" title="Halfino Berry"><img alt="Halfino Berry" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1204603980p2/171921.jpg"/></a>
<div class="left bodycol">
<div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
<a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2759571?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate">Nov 17, 2011</a>
<a class="user" href="/user/show/171921-halfino-berry" title="Halfino Berry">Halfino Berry</a>

        rated it
        <a class=" staticStars stars_4" title="really liked it">4 of 5 stars</a>
<span class="greyText"> · </span>
<a class="lightGreyText" href="/book/show/231622.And_Then_There_Were_None" title="Paperback 9780312979478">review of another edition</a>
<div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
<span class="uitext reviewText">mystery lovers</span></div>
<div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
                <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/171921-halfino-berry?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>

<div class="reviewText stacked">
<span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer2759571" style="">
<span id="freeTextContainer8895921630955011158">I read it many years ago, during my junior high (or before?), loved it, and consider it as one of Christie's best writing. <br><br>You won't find Poirot or Miss Marple in it, but as her other books are usually related to some popular rhymes, this one is related with '10 Little Indians' (which is the other title for this book).<br><br>Alternately, you will have these ten people with the dark past isolated in an island. One by one, each of them were killed. You may guess who the killer was while turning page over</br></br></br></br></span>
<span id="freeText8895921630955011158" style="display:none">I read it many years ago, during my junior high (or before?), loved it, and consider it as one of Christie's best writing. <br><br>You won't find Poirot or Miss Marple in it, but as her other books are usually related to some popular rhymes, this one is related with '10 Little Indians' (which is the other title for this book).<br><br>Alternately, you will have these ten people with the dark past isolated in an island. One by one, each of them were killed. You may guess who the killer was while turning page over page, but I can guarantee that you'll never know! You may read it so careful .... and then there were none. So, whodunnit?<br><br>I shouldn't tell it more, because this book is a one time reading; once you learn the twist, you'll agree that nothing like the first reading. you may want to read it again, but it wouldn't have the same feeling of surprise. you can say the same thing to Fight Club, The Usual Suspect, or The Sixth Sense. <br><br>So, if you are fond of mystery and never read this, you should dig it soon.<br><br>============================<br><br>Moral: be careful with your past, or better, be careful with what you sow today, because it will be your harvest in the future.</br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></span>
<a data-text-id="8895921630955011158" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<a href="/user/show/26011634-wyatt-thompson" style="font-weight:bold">Wyatt Thompson</a>
<span id="freeTextContainer12489568478899363768">I got the same feeling about this book, this was one of Christi's books. I felt like the suspect was almost too obvious that you still didn't see it c</span>
<span id="freeText12489568478899363768" style="display:none">I got the same feeling about this book, this was one of Christi's books. I felt like the suspect was almost too obvious that you still didn't see it coming. The way Christie set the mood in the book you could expect the storm and the loss of power to trap the guests on the island. Murphy's law was on the side of the killer. After reading I wonder if there was a way for any of the guests to break the rhyme and catch the killer. They did see the Rhyme, why not try to follow it and avoid all of the clues in it? I also thought it was like The Sixth Sense, you almost could say the ending, but you needed to know who did it. Overall this was a great book and i too recommend it.</span>

The most suspenseful parts of the book was when someone was unexpectedly killed.</span>

<div class="section">
<div class="review" id="review_270513309" itemprop="reviews" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
<link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/270513309" itemprop="url"/>
<a class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/111921-madeline" title="Madeline"><img alt="Madeline" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1220803522p2/111921.jpg"/></a>
<div class="left bodycol">
<div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
<a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/270513309?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate">Jan 31, 2012</a>
<a class="user" href="/user/show/111921-madeline" title="Madeline">Madeline</a>

        rated it
        <a class=" staticStars stars_4" title="really liked it">4 of 5 stars</a>
<div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
                <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/111921-madeline?shelf=detective-fiction">detective-fiction</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="reviewText stacked">
<span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer270513309" style="">
<span id="freeTextContainer16854540302026166002">“Ten little soldier boys went out to dine; One choked his little self and then there were nine.<br><br>Nine little soldier boys sat up very late; One overslept himself and then there were eight.<br><br>Eight little soldier boys travelling in Devon; One said he'd stay there and then there were seven.<br><br>Seven little soldier boys chopping up sticks; One chopped himself in halves and then there were six.<br><br>Six little soldier boys playing with a hive; A bumblebee stung one and then there were five.<br><br>Five little soldier boys</br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></span>
<span id="freeText16854540302026166002" style="display:none">“Ten little soldier boys went out to dine; One choked his little self and then there were nine.<br><br>Nine little soldier boys sat up very late; One overslept himself and then there were eight.<br><br>Eight little soldier boys travelling in Devon; One said he'd stay there and then there were seven.<br><br>Seven little soldier boys chopping up sticks; One chopped himself in halves and then there were six.<br><br>Six little soldier boys playing with a hive; A bumblebee stung one and then there were five.<br><br>Five little soldier boys going in for law; One got in Chancery and then there were four.<br><br>Four little soldier boys going out to sea; A red herring swallowed one and then there were three.<br><br>Three little soldier boys walking in the Zoo; A big bear hugged one and then there were two.<br><br>Two little soldier boys sitting in the sun; One got frizzled up and then there was one.<br><br>One little soldier boy left all alone; He went and hanged himself and then there were none."<br><br>Fun fact: this was originally published as <em>Ten Little Niggers</em>, then <em>Ten Little Indians</em>, before finally settling on the offensive-to-no-one (we hope) <em>And Then There Were None</em>. Proving, of course, that a) Christie's publishers probably know what they're doing and b) a story can be great enough to completely eclipse its unsavory past. <br><br>This is a good mystery. This is a really good mystery, particularly to people who are already familiar with Agatha Christie's work, because it's like no other Christie mystery I've read so far. There's no official detective investigating the case from an impersonal distance (so those sick of Poirot's smarmy lectures about his stupid little gray cells, or frustrated by Miss Marple's lack of direct involvement in her own cases, will have much to be thankful for here), and although the Agatha Christie Players are still here (the young governess, the old military man, the cocky playboy, the old spinster), they all have a dark edge to them that hasn't been seen in other Christie books. Because, of course, the ten main characters in this mystery have all committed murder at some point in their lives. Some of the deaths were accidental, others were deliberate, but they all have something in common: each murder occurred in such a way that it can't be proven in a legal setting, and each death is the reason these ten people are brought to Soldier Island by a mysterious guest. And then they start getting killed off one by one, and it's suspenseful and creepy and everything that the <em>Saw</em> movies aren't even smart enough to try imitating. Admittedly, I guessed a couple of the plot twists, but only in a very general sense (like, "oh, I bet one of the people who's died isn't actually dead, but I have no idea who it might be") so I was kept guessing until the end. <br><br>That being said, I do have to let people know that the ending is the kind of mystery ending that I hate the most: where nobody can figure out who the killer is, so he/she waits until the last page and then starts shouting, "You fools! I totally did it, and in case you don't believe me, I will now outline precisely how I managed to pull off every single aspect of my murderous scheme!" Blech. But everything before that was a damn good time, so I wasn't even that mad. </br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></span>
<a data-text-id="16854540302026166002" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
</span>
</div>

<a class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar" title="Kelly (and the Book Boar)"><img alt="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1420643161p2/11183856.jpg"/></a>
<div class="left bodycol">
<div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
<a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1031977746?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate">Aug 28, 2014</a>
<a class="user" href="/user/show/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar" title="Kelly (and the Book Boar)">Kelly (and the Book Boar)</a>

        rated it
        <a class=" staticStars stars_4" title="really liked it">4 of 5 stars</a>
<div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
                <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar?shelf=read-in-2014">read-in-2014</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="reviewText stacked">
<span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1031977746" style="">
<span id="freeTextContainer13640094834355429765">Find all of my reviews at:  <a href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br><br><strong>WARNING:  IF YOU DID NOT LIKE HARPER’S ISLAND CLICK AWAY PRONTO ‘CAUSE <em>THIS</em> STORY REMINDED ME OF <em>THAT</em> STORY AND  I’M GOING TO HARPER’S ISLAND THE POOP OUT OF THIS MO-FO</strong><br><br>Still here?  Okay, let’s get on with the show.<br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/5IBnWGl" rel="nofollow">
<img class="escapedImg" src="https://p.gr-assets.com/540x540/fit/hostedimages/1409242839/10953181.gif"/></a><br><br>Upon starting <em>And Then There Were None</em>, I found myself feeling extremely . . . giddy.  WTF is wrong with me?  Normal people don’t get all smiley when they begin a book where everyone and their dog is going to get murdered.  I need</br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></span>
<span id="freeText13640094834355429765" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at:  <a href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br><br><strong>WARNING:  IF YOU DID NOT LIKE HARPER’S ISLAND CLICK AWAY PRONTO ‘CAUSE <em>THIS</em> STORY REMINDED ME OF <em>THAT</em> STORY AND  I’M GOING TO HARPER’S ISLAND THE POOP OUT OF THIS MO-FO</strong><br><br>Still here?  Okay, let’s get on with the show.<br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/5IBnWGl" rel="nofollow">
<img class="escapedImg" src="https://p.gr-assets.com/540x540/fit/hostedimages/1409242839/10953181.gif"/></a><br><br>Upon starting <em>And Then There Were None</em>, I found myself feeling extremely . . . giddy.  WTF is wrong with me?  Normal people don’t get all smiley when they begin a book where everyone and their dog is going to get murdered.  I need professional help.<br><br>Generally in the summertime I follow a couple of traditions faithfully:<br><br>1.  I read a <strong>lot</strong> of nonsense while sitting poolside (preferably with a smuggled-in piña colada or margarita in hand); and<br><br>2.  I drive my husband nuts with my annual viewing of Harper’s Island.  (I have no clue how we’ve stayed married so long – he doesn’t like Harper’s Island, he doesn’t like Sharknado – I should be nominated for sainthood.)<br><br>This summer I’ve kind of broken free of the confines of Rule #1 - not saying I haven’t read some fluff, but I’ve been heavy handed in choosing more thriller/horror novels.  Maybe it was the abnormally cool temps that not only kept my toes out of the water, but also helped me keep my wits about me? <br><br>Whatever the cause, I’ve had some serious quality reading experiences over the past few months.  Endless thanks to <br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1020732520?book_show_action=false&amp;page=1"> twelvejan [Alexandria] </a> for bringing this classic tale to my attention.  I had read a handful of Poirot stories back in the Paleolithic Era, but found them to be just “okay”.  After reading <em>And Then There Were None</em>, I think it might possibly be Agatha Christie’s best work.  <br><br>Ten strangers, each with a skeleton in the closet, are summoned to an island by a host who only appears as a voice on a recording accusing the guests of murder.  What follows is the death of each person<br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/0T8q2iK" rel="nofollow">
<img class="escapedImg" src="https://p.gr-assets.com/540x540/fit/hostedimages/1409242839/10953182.gif"/></a><br><br>one<br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/WR2OciP" rel="nofollow">
<img class="escapedImg" src="https://p.gr-assets.com/540x540/fit/hostedimages/1409242839/10953183.gif"/></a><br><br>by one<br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/w33pNbj" rel="nofollow">
<img class="escapedImg" src="https://p.gr-assets.com/540x540/fit/hostedimages/1409242839/10953184.gif"/></a><br><br>by one<br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/eG10e8b" rel="nofollow">
<img class="escapedImg" src="https://p.gr-assets.com/540x540/fit/hostedimages/1409242839/10953185.gif"/></a><br><br>Until no one is left.<br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/Wt0jOLr" rel="nofollow">
<img class="escapedImg" src="https://p.gr-assets.com/540x540/fit/hostedimages/1409242839/10953186.gif"/></a><br><br>Okay, so maybe the murders aren’t <strong>
<em>that</em>
</strong> gruesome, but we are talking about a <strong>75 year old</strong> book here.  I was amazed at how well it stood the test of time and how it had me gripping the edge of my seat in anticipation.  And though, at the end of it all, you may claim to have known who the murderer was all along, you mustn’t forget all the times you changed your mind (because your choice of killer was one of the 10 little soldiers who happened to fall).<br><br>Recommended to?  Anyone looking for a quality murder mystery.<br><br>Now for a couple of wishlist items:<br><br>1.  It’s time for Harper’s Island 2.0.  Come on CBS, you know you wanna . . .<br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/Yas4hZ0" rel="nofollow">
<img class="escapedImg" src="https://p.gr-assets.com/540x540/fit/hostedimages/1409242839/10953187.gif"/></a><br><br>2.  Someone plan a murder mystery party and invite me.  My only requirement is that I get to wear a wedding gown and have the murderer chase me through the woods.<br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/q7I9O3N" rel="nofollow">
<img class="escapedImg" src="https://p.gr-assets.com/540x540/fit/hostedimages/1409242839/10953188.gif"/></a><br><br>You say you don’t live near any woods?  No problem – you can have the party at my house.  Just make sure you warn everyone that there are some REALLY weird looking dogs that occasionally hang out around the doghouse.<br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/WaojOIC" rel="nofollow">

        rated it
        <a class=" staticStars stars_5" title="it was amazing">5 of 5 stars</a>
<span class="greyText"> · </span>
<a class="lightGreyText" href="/book/show/231622.And_Then_There_Were_None" title="Paperback 9780312979478">review of another edition</a>
<div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

<div class="reviewText stacked">
<span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer45350872" style="">
<span id="freeTextContainer13555864528668005460">Made the mistake of starting this on the train ride home just now. Now it's 2am and HOLY MOLY DOES THIS BOOK HOLD UP! Was my favorite book in 5th grade and read it a ton of times then. I even know who the killer is and I'm still at the edge of my seat (or maybe more appropriately edge of my bed, under the covers with a booklight) Lordie. Someone pry this out of my hands and make me sleep!</span>
</span>

<span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1045688260" style="">
<span id="freeTextContainer609732860630114823"><br>من فترة وانا نفسي اقرأ حاجة لأجاثا كريستى <br>فقمت اشترت أشهر رواية لها عشان لو معجبتنيش قلت أكيد الباقى مش هيعجبنى<br><br>أول ما بدأت قراءة الرواية وعرفت الفكرة قلت ان الفكرة ده انا شفتها قبل كدا فى فيلم واتكررت<br>وأكيد الحبكة فى الرواية مش هتبقى جديدة وخصوصا أنها تم نشرها فى 1939<br>واتعمل بعدها كذا فيلم او رواية على نفس الفكرة<br><br>وكملت الرواية وعجبتنى جدا <br>الرواية والحبكة والاثارة لحد أخر سطر فى الرواية, والنهاية مش متوقعة<br><br>كل الحبكة والاثارة فى الرواية جميل لكن الصراحة قمة فى الابداع ان اجاثا تكتب الكلام ده فى 1939 ق</br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></span>
<span id="freeText609732860630114823" style="display:none"><br>من فترة وانا نفسي اقرأ حاجة لأجاثا كريستى <br>فقمت اشترت أشهر رواية لها عشان لو معجبتنيش قلت أكيد الباقى مش هيعجبنى<br><br>أول ما بدأت قراءة الرواية وعرفت الفكرة قلت ان الفكرة ده انا شفتها قبل كدا فى فيلم واتكررت<br>وأكيد الحبكة فى الرواية مش هتبقى جديدة وخصوصا أنها تم نشرها فى 1939<br>واتعمل بعدها كذا فيلم او رواية على نفس الفكرة<br><br>وكملت الرواية وعجبتنى جدا <br>الرواية والحبكة والاثارة لحد أخر سطر فى الرواية, والنهاية مش متوقعة<br><br>كل الحبكة والاثارة فى الرواية جميل لكن الصراحة قمة فى الابداع ان اجاثا تكتب الكلام ده فى 1939 قبل ما تظهر اى فكرة شبهها حتى<br>وأنها تعجبك فى سنة 2014 بعد ما الواحد شاف كذا فيلم ورواية نفس الفكرة<br><br>الصراحة عبقرية من أجاثا وخيال رائع لعمل تلك الرواية<br>سوف اقرأ لها قريبا بقية أعمالها ان شاء الله </br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></span>

<link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/135800611" itemprop="url"/>
<a class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4577698-buthy-ful" title="Buthy ful"><img alt="Buthy ful" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1322867597p2/4577698.jpg"/></a>
<div class="left bodycol">
<div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
<a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/135800611?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate">Dec 20, 2010</a>
<a class="user" href="/user/show/4577698-buthy-ful" title="Buthy ful">Buthy ful</a>

        rated it
        <a class=" staticStars stars_5" title="it was amazing">5 of 5 stars</a>
<span class="greyText"> · </span>
<a class="lightGreyText" href="/book/show/5051005" title="Paperback ">review of another edition</a>
<div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
                <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4577698-buthy-ful?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
                <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4577698-buthy-ful?shelf=a-must-read">a-must-read</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="reviewText stacked">
<span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer135800611" style="">
<span id="freeTextContainer7538995332824578140">ربما لم أقرأ لأحد كما قرأت لأجاثا كريستي وليس لأنها تكتب في الغموض والقصص البوليسية، ولكن لأنها تضيف دائماً البعد الإنساني لشخصياتها، وتضمن الصفحات آراءها في العدل والسياسة والحب والصراع بين الخير والشر..<br><br>هذه الرواية هي واحدة من أكثر من ثمانين كتبتها في الأدب البوليسي، وهي في رأيي مثل الدرة على التاج، فشخصياتها مصقولة وواضحة، وأحداثها متسلسلة. والتسلسل الزمني في الرواية حين تأخذنا الشخصيات في بحر الذكريات، يجعل القراءة مليئة بالإثارة.<br><br>أنصح بقراءتها لمحبي قصص الغموض</br></br></br></br></span>
</span>

<div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        rated it
        <a class=" staticStars stars_4" title="really liked it">4 of 5 stars</a>
<span class="greyText"> · </span>
<a class="lightGreyText" href="/book/show/10176670-and-then-there-were-none" title="ebook 9780061739255">review of another edition</a>

<div class="reviewText stacked">
<span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1175725616" style="">
<span id="freeTextContainer18393760041652784284"><strong>Miluju tu básničku...</strong> <br><br><em>Deset malých černoušků hostil děda Vševěd,<br>jeden z nich se zakuckal, zbylo jich jen devět.<br><br>Devět malých černoušků chtělo sypat kosům,<br>jeden se včas nevzbudil, zbylo jich jen osm.<br><br>Osm malých černoušků vyšlo si hrát před dům,<br>jeden z nich se potloukl, zbylo jich jen sedm.<br><br>Sedm malých černoušků šlo naštípat klest,<br>jeden z nich se posekal, zbylo jich jen šest.<br><br>Šest malinkých černoušků chtělo vybrat med,<br>čmelák píchl jednoho, zbylo jich jen pět.<br><br>Pět malinkých černoušků k soudu spolu míří,</br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></em></br></br></span>
<span id="freeText18393760041652784284" style="display:none"><strong>Miluju tu básničku...</strong> <br><br><em>Deset malých černoušků hostil děda Vševěd,<br>jeden z nich se zakuckal, zbylo jich jen devět.<br><br>Devět malých černoušků chtělo sypat kosům,<br>jeden se včas nevzbudil, zbylo jich jen osm.<br><br>Osm malých černoušků vyšlo si hrát před dům,<br>jeden z nich se potloukl, zbylo jich jen sedm.<br><br>Sedm malých černoušků šlo naštípat klest,<br>jeden z nich se posekal, zbylo jich jen šest.<br><br>Šest malinkých černoušků chtělo vybrat med,<br>čmelák píchl jednoho, zbylo jich jen pět.<br><br>Pět malinkých černoušků k soudu spolu míří,<br>jeden z nich se soudcem stal, zbyli jenom čtyři.<br><br>Čtyři malí černoušci nechali všech pří,<br>jeden z nich šel pasti klást, šli do světa tři.<br><br>Tři malincí černoušci šli ulovit lva,<br>medvěd sežral jednoho, zbyli jenom dva.<br><br>Dva malincí černoušci chodili dvě hodiny,<br>jeden klesl na skále, a tak zbyl jen jediný.<br><br>Jeden malý černoušek vztek měl na svět zrádný,<br>proto se sám oběsil - a tak nezbyl žádný.</br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></em><br/></br></br></span>

<div class="reviewText stacked">
<span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer763146" style="">
<span id="freeTextContainer12153219087754117746">A group of strangers is invited to a deserted island by a mysterious host they do not know. When they arrive they immediately <br>1. dislike each other<br>2. figure out that no one knows who the host is<br>3. discern that each person is hiding a dark secret<br>4. realize they were all blackmailed into coming<br>Then one by one, the guests begin to disappear. A short verse about 10 Little Indians appears at each crime scene. Those remaining frantically try to figure out what is going on.<br><br>This is my all-time favorite</br></br></br></br></br></br></br></span>
<span id="freeText12153219087754117746" style="display:none">A group of strangers is invited to a deserted island by a mysterious host they do not know. When they arrive they immediately <br>1. dislike each other<br>2. figure out that no one knows who the host is<br>3. discern that each person is hiding a dark secret<br>4. realize they were all blackmailed into coming<br>Then one by one, the guests begin to disappear. A short verse about 10 Little Indians appears at each crime scene. Those remaining frantically try to figure out what is going on.<br><br>This is my all-time favorite Agatha Christie mystery. The reason I liked it so much was that I could not figure out the ending until the last page, so it left me stunned! Many of her other novels (and I have read most of them!) were suspenseful but not this much of a nail-biter. </br></br></br></br></br></br></br></span>
<a data-text-id="12153219087754117746" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div class="review nosyndicate" id="review_468357512" itemprop="reviews" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
<link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/468357512" itemprop="url"/>
<a class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10923016-david-proud-member-of-branwen-s-adventuring-party" title="David &quot;proud member of Branwen's adventuring party&quot;"><img alt="David &quot;proud member of Branwen's adventuring party&quot;" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1417604800p2/10923016.jpg"/></a>
<div class="left bodycol">
<div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
<a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/468357512?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate">Jan 06, 2015</a>
<a class="user" href="/user/show/10923016-david-proud-member-of-branwen-s-adventuring-party" title="David &quot;proud member of Branwen's adventuring party&quot;">David "proud member of Branwen's adventuring party"</a>

        rated it
        <a class=" staticStars stars_5" title="it was amazing">5 of 5 stars</a>
<div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
                <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10923016-david-proud-member-of-branwen-s-adventuring-party?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
                <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10923016-david-proud-member-of-branwen-s-adventuring-party?shelf=favorite-books-or-series">favorite-books-or-series</a>, 
                <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10923016-david-proud-member-of-branwen-s-adventuring-party?shelf=five-inges-because-inge-is-a-star">five-inges-because-inge-is-a-star</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="reviewText stacked">
<span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer468357512" style="">
<span id="freeTextContainer152703846933787361">It's been a long time since I read this book...I was in my pre-teen years at the time!  Because of that, I really can't give too detailed a review, but I can honestly say that this was the novel that ignited my life-long love for mysteries!  Sure, as a kid, I had already been exposed to mysteries aimed at my age group...the Hardy Boys, Encyclopedia Brown, Scooby Doo (OK, that last one doesn't really count), but "And Then There Were None" was the first sophisticated mystery I ever read, and its eff</span>
<span id="freeText152703846933787361" style="display:none">It's been a long time since I read this book...I was in my pre-teen years at the time!  Because of that, I really can't give too detailed a review, but I can honestly say that this was the novel that ignited my life-long love for mysteries!  Sure, as a kid, I had already been exposed to mysteries aimed at my age group...the Hardy Boys, Encyclopedia Brown, Scooby Doo (OK, that last one doesn't really count), but "And Then There Were None" was the first sophisticated mystery I ever read, and its effects are still with me to this day.<br><br>'Lil 10-year-old Dave Green was completely entranced by so many things in this novel...the bizarre death-threat in the form of a poem, the feeling of dread and helplessness the potential victims all felt, the chilling murders, the twist ending.  I had read many books over the years, but this was the first book I actually FELT!  Fear, excitement, gloom, and even joy when I realized the author had completely fooled me in the final few pages.<br><br>Sometimes I consider rereading this book, but as corny as it sounds, I'm afraid that reading it a second time may take away some of the magic for me.  It's like when you watch an old movie you loved as a kid and find yourself saying, "This isn't nearly as good as I remembered!"  No, "And Then There was One" was a book that had a profound effect on me, and even though it's been over 25 years since I read it, it will always have a special place in my heart :)  </br></br></br></br></span>
<a data-text-id="152703846933787361" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
</span>

<div class="section">
<div class="review" id="review_23509853" itemprop="reviews" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
<link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/23509853" itemprop="url"/>
<a class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1205474-jason" title="Jason"><img alt="Jason" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1309897696p2/1205474.jpg"/></a>
<div class="left bodycol">
<div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
<a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/23509853?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate">Jun 02, 2008</a>
<a class="user" href="/user/show/1205474-jason" title="Jason">Jason</a>

        rated it
        <a class=" staticStars stars_4" title="really liked it">4 of 5 stars</a>
<div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
<span class="uitext reviewText">Mystery fans, aspiring screenwriters, everyone</span></div>
</div>
<div class="reviewText stacked">
<span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer23509853" style="">
<span id="freeTextContainer3811659522677932241">	I first read Christie a few weeks ago when I completed “Murder on the <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16304.Orient_Express" title="Orient Express by Agatha Christie">Orient Express</a>”. It blew me away, and I knew I would have to read more. “And Then There Were None” was a logical choice since it is so famous. My local library had a copy available for me.<br>	I do not think I have ever read through a book that quickly. It was very short, but very exciting! Agatha Christie does not disappoint in presenting not only a mystery that I did not figure out until the truth was told to me, but an engagin</br></span>
<span id="freeText3811659522677932241" style="display:none">	I first read Christie a few weeks ago when I completed “Murder on the <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16304.Orient_Express" title="Orient Express by Agatha Christie">Orient Express</a>”. It blew me away, and I knew I would have to read more. “And Then There Were None” was a logical choice since it is so famous. My local library had a copy available for me.<br>	I do not think I have ever read through a book that quickly. It was very short, but very exciting! Agatha Christie does not disappoint in presenting not only a mystery that I did not figure out until the truth was told to me, but an engaging thriller.<br>	It is the characters that make the story so amazing. With hardly any time spent on them in such a short book, all ten of the main characters came across as real and vibrant. After only a few pages I felt that I understood who they were, and what they wanted. Furthermore, I felt sorry for several of the characters even though they were, really, villains.<br>	Otherwise there is little to say for the story because it was so short. I suppose it suffices to say that it was one of the best short books I’ve ever read, and I am sure I will be reading it again.<br><br>4	Characters<br>	The characters are living and vibrant. They feel like unique individuals rather than cardboard cutouts. Furthermore, Christie was able to get me to care for the characters, and relate to them, even though they were all murderers in one way or another.<br><br>5	Pace<br>	No part of this book was boring or slow. As soon as the first page is read, a person finds themselves forced to continue. No time is wasted. The characters are introduced, put on the island, and then they start dying. The pace quickens as the murders continue… and I found myself missing work to continue reading.<br><br>4	Story<br>	The plot behind the story feels slightly thin- that a madman would lure nine people to an island to give them justice society could not, but it serves the concept and it works.<br><br>4	Dialogue<br>	The dialogue between characters is well written. I never questioned who was speaking at a given moment, though I did frequently wonder just who was thinking.<br><br>3	Style/Technical<br>	I wonder if the style is indicative of the times. There are many paragraph breaks that I would call needless, and she prefaces dialogue with a single, short paragraph identifying who was doing the speaking. It was never difficult and always clear, but did read strangely as a result. Her later works are not like that.<br><br>4	Overall<br>	This is a good book. I can understand why elements of it have been adapted to broadly for other books, comics, movies, and video games. I will be reading it again, if only to tap into the strange sense of unknown terror that it provides…</br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></span>
<a data-text-id="3811659522677932241" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
</span>
</div>

<a class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1713956-manny" title="Manny"><img alt="Manny" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1227275844p2/1713956.jpg"/></a>
<div class="left bodycol">
<div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
<a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/47586671?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate">Feb 26, 2009</a>
<a class="user" href="/user/show/1713956-manny" title="Manny">Manny</a>

        rated it
        <a class=" staticStars stars_4" title="really liked it">4 of 5 stars</a>
<span class="greyText"> · </span>
<a class="lightGreyText" href="/book/show/231622.And_Then_There_Were_None" title="Paperback 9780312979478">review of another edition</a>
</div>
<div class="reviewText stacked">
<span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer47586671" style="">
<span id="freeTextContainer12400090402554948459">My friend Amelie and I used this book as half of our corpus when we wrote our 1990 paper, <a href="http://acl.ldc.upenn.edu/J/J90/J90-2003.pdf" rel="nofollow">
<em>An Implementable Semantics for Comparative Constructions</em>
</a>. We spent several days combing through the text, extracting and categorizing every single occurrence of a comparative construction. So you'll appreciate that I know what I'm talking about when I say it's better than most murder mysteries.<br/></span>
</span>
