<div class="review" id="review_939214667" itemprop="reviews" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
<link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/939214667" itemprop="url"/>
<a class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4251871" title="حسام عادل"><img alt="حسام عادل" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1411752052p2/4251871.jpg"/></a>
<div class="left bodycol">
<div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
<a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/939214667?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate">Dec 25, 2014</a>
<a class="user" href="/user/show/4251871" title="حسام عادل">حسام عادل</a>

        rated it
        <a class=" staticStars stars_5" title="it was amazing">5 of 5 stars</a>
<div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
                <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4251871?shelf=tablet-pdf">tablet-pdf</a>, 
                <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4251871?shelf=%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%B1%D9%88%D8%A7%D8%A6%D8%B9">الروائع</a>, 
                <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4251871?shelf=agatha-christie">agatha-christie</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="reviewText stacked">
<span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer939214667" style="">
<span id="freeTextContainer4871516084070865006"><strong>تاج لاين تلك الرواية هى جملة:<br>------ خطيئتك سوف تلاحقك إلى الأبد ------<br><br>لا تحسب أن ما فعلته خاطئاً سيختفي,لا تظن أن جريمتك قد تتراكم عليها أتربة السنين وتخفيها عن العيون,فلعل كلمة,إشارة,ذكرى,تعيد إحياء ما دُفن قبل أعوام..وتبدأ مطاردة دموية لفريسة هي أنت..مطاردة لن تُكتب النهاية لها إلا بأحرف من دمك.<br><br><u>ملحوظة هامة: التالي لا يوجد به أى حرق للرواية وأحداثها بتاتاً فلا تقلق.</u><br><br>تحكى الرواية عن مجموعة من أبسط أنواع البشر التي قد تقابلها يوماً,لا تحسب أنك قد تجد فيهم مجرماً أو قاتلاً محترفاً أو حتى من يثير اه</br></br></br></br></br></br></br></strong></span>
<span id="freeText4871516084070865006" style="display:none"><strong>تاج لاين تلك الرواية هى جملة:<br>------ خطيئتك سوف تلاحقك إلى الأبد ------<br><br>لا تحسب أن ما فعلته خاطئاً سيختفي,لا تظن أن جريمتك قد تتراكم عليها أتربة السنين وتخفيها عن العيون,فلعل كلمة,إشارة,ذكرى,تعيد إحياء ما دُفن قبل أعوام..وتبدأ مطاردة دموية لفريسة هي أنت..مطاردة لن تُكتب النهاية لها إلا بأحرف من دمك.<br><br><u>ملحوظة هامة: التالي لا يوجد به أى حرق للرواية وأحداثها بتاتاً فلا تقلق.</u><br><br>تحكى الرواية عن مجموعة من أبسط أنواع البشر التي قد تقابلها يوماً,لا تحسب أنك قد تجد فيهم مجرماً أو قاتلاً محترفاً أو حتى من يثير اهتمامك بمغامراته..<br>جميعهم عاديين مملين لأقصى حد..<br>قاضٍ سابق,مدرسة,طبيب,جنرال متقاعد,ربة بيت...إلخ<br><br>ترتحل  تلك الجماعة إلى وجهة واحدة,وكل واحد منهم لا يعرف الآخر ولا يظن أنه يرافقه إلى نفس الوجهة حتى...إلى جزيرة الجنود الغامضة<br><br>كما تباينت شخصياتهم تباينت أيضاً أسباب حضورهم للجزيرة التى لم يقابل أحد صاحبها أبداً ولم يعرف عنه سوى اسمه فقط,انقسموا مابين مَن حضر مدعواً لحفل وآخر لشغل وظيفة وآخر للتأمين...إلخ<br><br>فجأة تنقلب الأحداث رأساً على عقب ودون مقدمات..يدوي ذلك الصوت الآمر القوي المهيب في أرجاء القصر مواجهاً كل فرد من تلك المجموعة بجريمة غامضة سرية قديمة له لم تُكتشف أو يعرف عنها أحد أبداً,ثم يختتم الصوت بسقوط أول الضحايا ميتاً..<br>حينها يعرف الجميع أن الأمر ليس مزحة وأنهم قد حضروا فقط كي تتم محاكمتهم..والحكم جاهز:الإعدام لكل واحد منهم بالترتيب..حتى تأتي النهاية ولا يتبق أحد<br><br>التيمة الأساسية - كما قرأت - ليست فريدة من نوعها,أعتقد أنها قد مرت علي في عدد محترم من الأفلام,لكن في زمن كتابتها وبهذا الإسلوب الاحترافي المذهل تستحق فعلاً تصفيق حار لسيدة عالم الجريمة والروايات البوليسية<br><br>لمدة أربع ساعات كاملة كنت أتعلق بهاتفي غير قادر على النهوض وإضاعة وقت من الرواية في أعمال تافهة كشرب الماء حتى!!..أقفز بعيني على السطور متلهفاً وقلبي يخفق فى عنف..ماذا سيحدث لاحقاً؟ من فعلها؟ كيف تكون النهاية؟..<br>الحق أني كنت مسحوراً بهذا العالم الغريب المثير المحكم بعناية فائقة..لا مشهد زائد..لا حوار ممل..كل شىء فى مكانه ومحسوب ومرتب بدقة تثير الغيظ..حتى التفصيلات الصغيرة التى قد تفوتها أنت نفسك كقارىء لا تهرب من يد كريستي وتذكرك بها في النهاية لتجد نفسك تهتف: كيف فاتني ذلك؟؟<br>حتى الإسلوب كان ممتعاً لأقصى درجة بمشاهد السينمائية المقطعة التي تجعلك تلهث من سرعة الإيقاع وتشويقه..لا أحسب أني قرأت رواية بوليسية متماسكة وممتعة من الألف للياء بإسلوب ساحر كتلك الرواية من قبل<br><br>إنتهاءً:الرواية من أفضل الروايات البوليسية التى قرأتها فى حياتي على الإطلاق..اقرأوها فهي تستحق فعلاً..أما عني فدعوني أبحث عن الرواية التالية لأغاثا كريستي<br><br>بالله كيف كنت جاهلاً ولم أقرأ لتلك السيدة قبلاً؟ :)</br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></strong></span>
<a data-text-id="4871516084070865006" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div class="review nosyndicate" id="review_583496069" itemprop="reviews" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
<link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/583496069" itemprop="url"/>
<a class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6536286-ariel" title="Ariel"><img alt="Ariel" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1414870774p2/6536286.jpg"/></a>
<div class="left bodycol">
<div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
<a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/583496069?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate">Apr 14, 2013</a>
<a class="user" href="/user/show/6536286-ariel" title="Ariel">Ariel</a>

        rated it
        <a class=" staticStars stars_4" title="really liked it">4 of 5 stars</a>
<span class="greyText"> · </span>
<a class="lightGreyText" href="/book/show/181132.And_Then_There_Were_None" title="Paperback 9780671417550">review of another edition</a>
</div>
<div class="reviewText stacked">
<span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer583496069" style="">
<span id="freeTextContainer10120252856829413513">I am so glad that I finally picked up an Agatha Christie.. it was about time, and I think that I chose a good one to start with! And Then There Were None, fun fact, is the best-selling mystery novel in all of human history!<br><br>Overall, I thought that this was an excellent novel. It was very intriguing, and by half way I didn't want to put it down - I needed to know what was going on! I definitely understand why Christie is held in such high regard, too: her writing is quick and on edge, it's realist</br></br></span>
<span id="freeText10120252856829413513" style="display:none">I am so glad that I finally picked up an Agatha Christie.. it was about time, and I think that I chose a good one to start with! And Then There Were None, fun fact, is the best-selling mystery novel in all of human history!<br><br>Overall, I thought that this was an excellent novel. It was very intriguing, and by half way I didn't want to put it down - I needed to know what was going on! I definitely understand why Christie is held in such high regard, too: her writing is quick and on edge, it's realistic, and she did a brilliant job with the intricacies. I really enjoyed this and I definitely want to read more from her.<br><br>Obviously though, I had a few problems with it if I didn't give it 5 stars! Firstly, I'm not completely sold on the ending. I think the whole "red herring" thing was BRILLIANT, completely didn't see that twist coming, but I'm just left unsatisfied. I don't know what I wanted, but I don't feel like I totally got it. Secondly, I never had any suspicions. One thing that I really like about mysteries is blaming people ("IT'S THAT GUY, OBVIOUSLY PEEPS!") and then changing your mind and doubting yourself. But I really didn't feel that in this novel.. I never blamed anyone, never had any leading ideas as to who it might have been which was too bad because I didn't feel like I was trying to solve this crime: There wasn't enough evidence or clues to help me along to figuring it out. These are both personal issues though, so objectively, I'd probably give it a higher rating!<br><br>Bonus: I REALLY SUPER DUPER LOVED the use of the nursery rhyme. Even though you know exactly how the next murder is going to happen you still have no idea and that was intriguing! </br></br></br></br></br></br></span>
<a data-text-id="10120252856829413513" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
</span>
</div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6248824935305987403"><strong> 4.5 Stars </strong><br><br>And then there were none by Agatha Christie.<br><br>Having never read an Agatha Christie novel I was delighted to get my hands on this book as it's title alone is intriguing.<br><br>This novel was published in 1939 and I thought while it might be a good read it would be a little out of date and may not live up to it's popularity of the time.  How wrong I was, this novel is still as fresh and interesting as any modern mystery if not more so.<br><br>The story of 10 strangers, each lured to Soldier Island by a m</br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></span>
<span id="freeText6248824935305987403" style="display:none"><strong> 4.5 Stars </strong><br><br>And then there were none by Agatha Christie.<br><br>Having never read an Agatha Christie novel I was delighted to get my hands on this book as it's title alone is intriguing.<br><br>This novel was published in 1939 and I thought while it might be a good read it would be a little out of date and may not live up to it's popularity of the time.  How wrong I was, this novel is still as fresh and interesting as any modern mystery if not more so.<br><br>The story of 10 strangers, each lured to Soldier Island by a mysterious host.  Once the guests arrive the host accuses each person of murder. The guests are unable to leave the Island, and so begins the sharing of their darkest secrets and then the mysterious deaths occur.<br><br>I loved everything about this novel from the old fashioned prose to the wonderful imaginative plot.  The Characters are brilliantly written and masterly crafted by Christie. The suspense is intriguing and had me guessing all along.<br><br>A wonderful read and a book that deserves all the praise that it has received.  All I can say is.......................................<br><strong> What took me so long to read this wonderful book.  </strong></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></span>
<a data-text-id="6248824935305987403" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
</span>

<link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/148714509" itemprop="url"/>
<a class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4807118-cheryl" title="Cheryl"><img alt="Cheryl" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1309134222p2/4807118.jpg"/></a>
<div class="left bodycol">
<div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
<a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/148714509?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate">Jan 07, 2012</a>
<a class="user" href="/user/show/4807118-cheryl" title="Cheryl">Cheryl</a>

        rated it
        <a class=" staticStars stars_5" title="it was amazing">5 of 5 stars</a>
<span class="greyText"> · </span>
<a class="lightGreyText" href="/book/show/6251563-and-then-there-were-none" title="Kindle Edition ">review of another edition</a>
<div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
                <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4807118-cheryl?shelf=kindle-edition">kindle-edition</a>, 
                <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4807118-cheryl?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
                <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4807118-cheryl?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>

<div class="reviewText stacked">
<span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer148714509" style="">
<span id="freeTextContainer15684265451658942576">Recognition is essential in the mind of a serial killer, and though pathological to an extreme, the resolution of the crimes on Indian Island would still elude me without the motive, means, and process described in the epilogue of Agatha Christie's AND THEN THERE WERE NONE. <br><br>With the nursery rhyme Ten Little Indians echoing in the reader's mind, ten invited visitors to the Island, unknown to one another, are viciously murdered in a few blustering days in August.<br><br>Each holds a secret of crimes commi</br></br></br></br></span>
<span id="freeText15684265451658942576" style="display:none">Recognition is essential in the mind of a serial killer, and though pathological to an extreme, the resolution of the crimes on Indian Island would still elude me without the motive, means, and process described in the epilogue of Agatha Christie's AND THEN THERE WERE NONE. <br><br>With the nursery rhyme Ten Little Indians echoing in the reader's mind, ten invited visitors to the Island, unknown to one another, are viciously murdered in a few blustering days in August.<br><br>Each holds a secret of crimes committed and punishment escaped. Who knows the secrets, is sadistically planning retribution with a rationalization of justice?<br><br>Were I to have lived during the life of Ms. Christie and on occasion been in a remote spot in a summer gale, I would wonder what secrets she had on me and be very fearful! <br><br>Such is the impact, even with a second reading, of this impossibly written tangled web of intrique and murder. Highest Recommendation!</br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></span>

        rated it

<span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer712789390" style="">
<span id="freeTextContainer7674872398512858755"><img class="escapedImg" height="250" src="https://p.gr-assets.com/540x540/fit/hostedimages/1380435680/880355.jpg" width="400"><br><em>Image courtesy of Wikipedia.org (*In my opinion* Left to right: Blore, Wargrave, Armstrong, Rogers, Lombard, Macarthur)</em><br><br><strong>Breathtaking, tragic, climactic</strong><br><br>A crazy murder classic. This is my first time to try a Christie novel but the suspense behind And Then There Were None got me shifting on my seat (quite intense criminology) as characters get killed by a mysterious murderer one by one.<br><br>When I read that Ten Little Indians poem, I knew it - in that part I'm right, however I still kept guessing who's w</br></br></br></br></br></br></br></img></span>
<span id="freeText7674872398512858755" style="display:none"><img class="escapedImg" height="250" src="https://p.gr-assets.com/540x540/fit/hostedimages/1380435680/880355.jpg" width="400"><br><em>Image courtesy of Wikipedia.org (*In my opinion* Left to right: Blore, Wargrave, Armstrong, Rogers, Lombard, Macarthur)</em><br><br><strong>Breathtaking, tragic, climactic</strong><br><br>A crazy murder classic. This is my first time to try a Christie novel but the suspense behind And Then There Were None got me shifting on my seat (quite intense criminology) as characters get killed by a mysterious murderer one by one.<br><br>When I read that Ten Little Indians poem, I knew it - in that part I'm right, however I still kept guessing who's who 'til the end (guess in some parts I didn't expect it coming) so big pat on the back to Agatha Christie for the mind games she gave me. In fact, her writing is easily adaptable despite the classic slang and prose because I enjoyed the conversations, the fast-paced comically-relevant murders, especially how she depicted each character very well in various tones, attitudes and ages. <br><br>I'll be reading more of her novels because of this! :) <br><br><img class="escapedImg" height="250" src="https://p.gr-assets.com/540x540/fit/hostedimages/1380435680/880356.jpg" width="400"><em>So, will you come to the Indian island?</em><br><br>PS. Thanks Juks!</br></br></img></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></img></span>

<div class="section">
<div class="review" id="review_792862394" itemprop="reviews" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
<link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/792862394" itemprop="url"/>
<a class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4015835-michael" title="Michael"><img alt="Michael" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1420385695p2/4015835.jpg"/></a>
<div class="left bodycol">
<div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
<a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/792862394?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate">Dec 30, 2013</a>
<a class="user" href="/user/show/4015835-michael" title="Michael">Michael</a>

        rated it
        <a class=" staticStars stars_3" title="liked it">3 of 5 stars</a>
<div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
                <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4015835-michael?shelf=1930s">1930s</a>, 
                <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4015835-michael?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
                <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4015835-michael?shelf=book-club-literary-exploration">book-club-literary-exploration</a>, 
                <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4015835-michael?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
</div>
</div>
<div class="reviewText stacked">
<span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer792862394" style="">
<span id="freeTextContainer7181451002994160072">Ten people have been invited to have a holiday on Soldier Island; when they arrived they thought they had nothing in common. Soon they find out all of them have become complacent with the death (or deaths) of other human beings. One by one they all die, but who is the one that is there to seek revenge on the others?<br><br>And Then There Were None was originally titled Ten Little (I would rather not say) after the British nursery rhyme. The US edition used this title (which is also the last line of the</br></br></span>
<span id="freeText7181451002994160072" style="display:none">Ten people have been invited to have a holiday on Soldier Island; when they arrived they thought they had nothing in common. Soon they find out all of them have become complacent with the death (or deaths) of other human beings. One by one they all die, but who is the one that is there to seek revenge on the others?<br><br>And Then There Were None was originally titled Ten Little (I would rather not say) after the British nursery rhyme. The US edition used this title (which is also the last line of the rhyme) as well as changing the song to Ten Little Indians. Once again the novel was revived and now the song title has been changed to Ten Little Soldiers. Apart from the offensive name of the book originally, this novel was wildly successful and introduced a very common crime trope into the world. Ten people trapped in a house on an island trying to work out who is killing them off one by one. I’m sure you can think of many films, shows and books that have paid homage to this theme.<br><br>This classic crime novel looks at the idea of administrating justice; who has the right to judge others, and what happens when the law fails. I’m going to try to avoid spoilers and tell you who the killer is but most people would have read this and probably remember who the perpetrator was. The killer believes the others are complacent and in most facts while they deny being guilty publically are living tormented lives. Not everyone, but it was interesting to see that kind of turmoil and I was a little upset to see that wasn’t explored in greater detail. Having said that, I think the torment played out more in the symbolism and motifs. I’m thinking about the dreams and hallucinations (the guilty consciences of the victims are explored here) or the storm; a symbol of violence that cuts them off from the world.<br><br>The killer has set out to commit the perfect crime and it looks good on paper but I never really bought into it. While reading this novel I had a feeling that the cosy crime approach is playing against the story. If you think about the mess made from the violent murders, wouldn’t help the police work out what happened in the end? I’m sure they wouldn’t rely on the handwritten accounts, the evidence would be inconsistent. Making this far from a perfect crime (sorry this is hard to explain without spoilers).<br><br>This was my first Agatha Christie novel and while I enjoyed it there is one thing that frustrated me. I hate crime novels that hold back important pieces of evidence and expect the reader to work out what happened. I always feel like the author is trying to be smug but really it is just poorly executed writing. It wasn’t so bad in this novel but I get the feeling it is a common occurrence in all her novels and I can’t stand that. You have to make a great protagonist to make up for the withholding of information. It works better as a first person narrative; the unreliable narrator is more likely to forget to tell you important clues.<br><br>I will read some more Christie, I hope I’m mistaken about the withholding of clues. And Then There Were None had no real protagonist but maybe a Hercule Poirot, Miss Jane Marple or Tommy and Tuppence mystery hide this a little better. I suspect Murder on the Orient Express will be my next Agatha Christie read but who knows. I prefer my detectives a little more Hard-Boiled so it might be awhile between Christie novels.<br><br>This review originally appeared on my blog; <a href="http://literary-exploration.com/2013/12/29/book-of-the-month-and-then-there-were-none/" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">http://literary-exploration.com/2013/...</a></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></span>
<a data-text-id="7181451002994160072" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
</span>

<a class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5277704-chiara-pagliochini" title="Chiara Pagliochini"><img alt="Chiara Pagliochini" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1364825157p2/5277704.jpg"/></a>

<div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
<a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/184216560?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate">Jul 12, 2011</a>
<a class="user" href="/user/show/5277704-chiara-pagliochini" title="Chiara Pagliochini">Chiara Pagliochini</a>

        rated it
        <a class=" staticStars stars_5" title="it was amazing">5 of 5 stars</a>
<span class="greyText"> · </span>
<a class="lightGreyText" href="/book/show/3400019-dieci-piccoli-indiani" title="Paperback 9788804307679">review of another edition</a>
<div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
                <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5277704-chiara-pagliochini?shelf=gialli">gialli</a>,

<div class="reviewText stacked">
<span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer184216560" style="">
<span id="freeTextContainer16935046615571010238"><br>Dieci piccoli indiani è probabilmente il miglior libro di Agatha Christie (a proposito, sapevate che era dislessica?). <br>Innanzitutto, è una pecora nera nella produzione della Christie, e questo a causa della sua marcata amoralità. Conosciamo Miss Marple ed Hercule Poirot e siamo abituati ad aspettarci che i due investigatori si trovino sulla scena di un delitto, scoprano il colpevole e lo smascherino. <br>Ebbene, qui tutti questi elementi vengono meno: sono tutti colpevoli, non ci sono investigatori,</br></br></br></span>
<span id="freeText16935046615571010238" style="display:none"><br>Dieci piccoli indiani è probabilmente il miglior libro di Agatha Christie (a proposito, sapevate che era dislessica?). <br>Innanzitutto, è una pecora nera nella produzione della Christie, e questo a causa della sua marcata amoralità. Conosciamo Miss Marple ed Hercule Poirot e siamo abituati ad aspettarci che i due investigatori si trovino sulla scena di un delitto, scoprano il colpevole e lo smascherino. <br>Ebbene, qui tutti questi elementi vengono meno: sono tutti colpevoli, non ci sono investigatori, nessuno smascheramento o punizione finale. <br>Dieci persone dal passato oscuro, ognuna delle quali si è resa responsabile di un delitto ed è riuscita a sfuggire alle maglie della legge, vengono convocate con un pretesto su un’isola da un misterioso ricco signore. Moriranno uno ad uno, uccisi da un giustiziere invisibile che segue alla lettera i versi di una filastrocca, quella dei Dieci Piccoli Indiani per l’appunto. È il noto schema di “delitto in villa chiusa”, che gli sciagurati adoratori di cartoni animati come me troveranno molto ricorrente anche in Conan. <br>I personaggi creati dall’autrice in questo libro sono molto diversi di quelli che ci aspetteremmo da lei. Hanno più spessore del solito, ad esempio: sono tormentati, ombrosi, ambigui. Si muovono in un clima di paura e di accusa che li spinge a mettersi uno contro l’altro, perché ignorano chi sia il loro nemico. <br>Un giallo angosciante, da cui non riuscirete a staccarvi, a mio avviso superiore anche al tanto celebre Assassinio sull’Orient Express (anche quello curiosamente bello e amorale, ma io sono allergica a Poirot, etciù). <br>Adoro la Christie, nulla da aggiungere. La preferisco decisamente a Conan Doyle; il caro Sherlock non riesce a conquistarmi: lui sa sempre tutto e a noi lettori non lascia che le briciole del suo acume. A me, invece, piace troppo giocare ad indovinare. <br/></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></span>
<a data-text-id="16935046615571010238" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
</span>

<div class="xhr_comment_body">
<a href="/user/show/5393355-esdaile" style="font-weight:bold">Esdaile</a>
<span id="freeTextContainer11645432040390093883">Bene dito! Mi interesse a leggere che in italiano se parla de "dieci indiani", una parte della tendenza di cambiare anchè gli titoli degli libri tropp</span>
<span id="freeText11645432040390093883" style="display:none">Bene dito! Mi interesse a leggere che in italiano se parla de "dieci indiani", una parte della tendenza di cambiare anchè gli titoli degli libri troppo "incorretto". Come se chaime la insola nellow verzione chiamata "dieci indiani"? Domando perchè nella versione originale la insola se chiame "nigger island". Si chiame forse "insola indiana"? E cossi schiocco no è vero? dopo uneo film di "ten little Indians" erana protesti contra la parola "indiano" e se ha cambiato ancora una volta e abbiamo adesso "and then there was none" che no e corretto della vista grammatica. Se deve essere secondo me "and then there was none."</span>

Having published The<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText10702190392899746136\" style=\"display:none\">The Return of Sherlock Holmes is a collection of 13 Sherlock Holmes stories, originally published in 1903-1904, by Arthur Conan Doyle. This was the first Holmes collection since 1893, when Holmes had &quot;died&quot; in The Final Problem. Having published The Hound of the Baskervilles in 1901-1902 (although setting it before Holmes\' death) Doyle came under intense pressure to revive his famous character. The first story is set in 1894 and has Holmes returning in London and explaining the period from 1891-94, a period called &quot;The Great Hiatus&quot; by Sherlockian enthusiasts. Also of note is Watson\'s statement in the last story of the cycle that Holmes has retired, and forbids him to publish any more stories.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"10702190392899746136\" href=\"#\" <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/123715.Agatha_Christie">About Agatha Christie</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
<a href="/author/show/123715.Agatha_Christie"><img alt="123715" class="right" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1321738793p2/123715.jpg"/></a>
<div class="readable">
<span id="freeTextContainer9862204248896176113">Agatha Christie also wrote romance novels under the pseudonym <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/author/show/10058.Mary_Westmacott" title="Mary Westmacott">Mary Westmacott</a>, and was occasionally published under the name <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7044774.Agatha_Christie_Mallowan" title="Agatha Christie Mallowan">Agatha Christie Mallowan</a>.<br><br>Agatha Mary Clarissa Miller was born in Torquay, Devon, England, U.K., as the youngest of three. The Millers had two other children: Margaret Frary Miller (1879–1950), called Madge, who was eleven years Agatha's senior, and Louis Montant Miller (1880</br></br></span>
<span id="freeText9862204248896176113" style="display:none">Agatha Christie also wrote romance novels under the pseudonym <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/author/show/10058.Mary_Westmacott" title="Mary Westmacott">Mary Westmacott</a>, and was occasionally published under the name <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7044774.Agatha_Christie_Mallowan" title="Agatha Christie Mallowan">Agatha Christie Mallowan</a>.<br><br>Agatha Mary Clarissa Miller was born in Torquay, Devon, England, U.K., as the youngest of three. The Millers had two other children: Margaret Frary Miller (1879–1950), called Madge, who was eleven years Agatha's senior, and Louis Montant Miller (1880–1929), called Monty, ten years older than Agatha. <br><br>During the First World War, she worked at a hospital as a nurse; later working at a hospital pharmacy, a job that influenced her work, as many of the murders in her books are carried out with poison.<br><br>On Christmas Eve 1914 Agatha married Archibald Christie, an aviator in the Royal Flying Corps. The couple had one daughter, Rosalind Hicks. They divorced in 1928, two years after Christie discovered her husband was having an affair.<br><br>Her first novel, The Mysterious Affair at Styles, came out in 1920. During this marriage, Agatha published six novels, a collection of short stories, and a number of short stories in magazines.<br><br>In late 1926, Agatha's husband, Archie, revealed that he was in love with another woman, Nancy Neele, and wanted a divorce. On 8 December 1926 the couple quarreled, and Archie Christie left their house Styles in Sunningdale, Berkshire, to spend the weekend with his mistress at Godalming, Surrey. That same evening Agatha disappeared from her home, leaving behind a letter for her secretary saying that she was going to Yorkshire. Her disappearance caused an outcry from the public, many of whom were admirers of her novels. Despite a massive manhunt, she was not found for eleven days.<br><br>In 1930, Christie married archaeologist Max Mallowan (Sir Max from 1968) after joining him in an archaeological dig. Their marriage was especially happy in the early years and remained so until Christie's death in 1976. In 1977, Mallowan married his longtime associate, Barbara Parker.<br><br>Christie frequently used familiar settings for her stories. Christie's travels with Mallowan contributed background to several of her novels set in the Middle East. Other novels (such as And Then There Were None) were set in and around Torquay, where she was born. Christie's 1934 novel Murder on the Orient Express was written in the Hotel Pera Palace in Istanbul, Turkey, the southern terminus of the railway. The hotel maintains Christie's room as a memorial to the author. The Greenway Estate in Devon, acquired by the couple as a summer residence in 1938, is now in the care of the National Trust.<br><br>Christie often stayed at Abney Hall in Cheshire, which was owned by her brother-in-law, James Watts. She based at least two of her stories on the hall: the short story The Adventure of the Christmas Pudding, which is in the story collection of the same name, and the novel After the Funeral. "Abney became Agatha's greatest inspiration for country-house life, with all the servants and grandeur which have been woven into her plots.<br><br>During the Second World War, Christie worked in the pharmacy at University College Hospital of University College, London, where she acquired a knowledge of poisons that she put to good use in her post-war crime novels.  <br><br>To honour her many literary works, she was appointed Commander of the Order of the British Empire in the 1956 New Year Honours. The next year, she became the President of the Detection Club. In the 1971 New Year Honours she was promoted Dame Commander of the Order of the British Empire, three years after her husband had been knighted for his archeological work in 1968.<br><br><a href="http://us.macmillan.com/author/agathachristie-author" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">http://us.macmillan.com/author/agatha...</a></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></br></span>
<a data-text-id="9862204248896176113" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
</div>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/3038872-ten-little-niggers">Quotes from Ten Little Indians</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
<div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
<span class="readable">“Ten little Indian boys went out to dine; One choked his little self and then there were nine.<br/>Nine little Indian boys sat up very late; One overslept himself and then there were eight.<br/>Eight little Indian boys travelling in Devon; One said he'd stay there and then there were seven.<br/>Seven little Indian boys chopping up sticks; One chopped himself in halves and then there were six. <br/>Six little Indian boys playing with a hive; A bumblebee stung one and then there were five.<br/>Five little Indian boys going in for law; One got in Chancery and then there were four.<br/>Four little Indian boys going out to sea; A red herring swallowed one and then there were three. <br/>Three little Indian boys walking in the Zoo; A big bear hugged one and then there were two.<br/>Two little Indian boys sitting in the sun; One got frizzled up and then there was one.<br/>One little Indian boy left all alone; He went and hanged himself and then there were none.”</span>
<nobr>
            —
            <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/300480-ten-little-indian-boys-went-out-to-dine-one-choked">316 likes</a>
</nobr>

</div>
<div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
